To do this, you can use VLANs (Virtual LANs) to isolate the devices on the remaining subnetworks from each other, while still allowing them to communicate with each other through the core switches.\n\nHere's how you can do it:\n\n1. Create a new VLAN for the devices that were previously on the removed subnetwork. This will isolate them from the rest of the network, but they will still be able to communicate with each other through the core switches.\n2. Configure the core switches to allow traffic from the new VLAN to pass through to the remaining subnetworks. This can be done by setting up access control lists (ACLs) on the core switches to filter incoming traffic based on the VLAN ID of the packets.\n3. Update the IP address configuration for the devices on the new VLAN to use IP addresses from the new VLAN range. This will ensure that they are reachable only within the new VLAN and cannot be reached directly from the rest of the network.\n4. Configure the routing protocols to advertise the new VLAN to the rest of the network, so that traffic can still flow between the new VLAN and the remaining subnetworks through the core switches.\n\nBy following these steps, you can remove one subnetwork while keeping all the devices able to ping each other, without disrupting their connectivity to the rest of the network."}

Create a new subnetwork that includes all the devices from the original subnetwork:\n```\nnew_subnet = {'id': 'new_subnet', 'nodes': [...], 'links': [...]}\n```\n2. Remove the original subnetwork:\n```\ndel network['subnetworks'][0]\n```\n3. Update the links to point to the new subnetwork:\n```\nfor link in network['links']:\n    if link['source'] in network['subnetworks']:\n        link['source'] = 'new_subnet'\n        link['target'] = link['target']\n```\n4. Save the updated network:\n```\nnetwork['links'] = [link for link in network['links'] if link['source'] != 'new_subnet']\n```\nAfter these steps, all the devices should be able to ping each other even though one subnetwork has been removed.
